SLCARP Annual Report 2019

ASia Pacific Association of Agricultural Research Institute (APAARI)

SLCARP has been a member of APAARI since its inception and pays an annual
membership fee. Secretary SLCARP was an executive committee member for years and
Chairman appointed an executive member Asian Pacific Consortium on Biotechnology and
Bio resources (APCOB). Since its establishment APAARI has significantly contributed
towards addressing agricultural research needs and enhancing food and nutritional security
in the region. The close links, networks, partnerships and collaboration with stakeholders
that APAARI has developed over the years, makes the Association a valuable organization
in the region. The ultimate aim of APAARI is to help realizing sustainable development
goals in Asia and the Pacific. Through the Asia Pacific Association for Agricultural
Research Institutions (APAARL), two training and invitation for a workshop were offered

to SLCARP which are given below along with names of participants:

SLCARP Annual Report 2019

MoU between SLCARP and Malaysian Agricultural Research and Development Institute

SLCARP and Malaysian Agricultural Research and Development Institute (MARDI) have entered
into a Memorandum of Understanding (MoU) ou scientific and technical cooperation and
development of Human Resource of agricultural scientists in the National Agricultural Research
System (NARS) in 2016 when His Excellency the President of Sri Lanka Visits Malaysia. The
objective of the MoU is to strengthen, facilitate, promote and develop scientific and technical
cooperation between the participants with an emphasis for the enhancement of cooperation for
mutual benefits to take necessary steps to encourage, facilitate and promote scientific and technical
cooperation in the areas of; Agriculture, Livestock and Information Management System in
Agriculture. For the year 2019, a need assessment was conducted to identify the local training
requirement by sending a requesting letter to the heads of the NARS by asking required training
needs. Training needs were conveyed to MARDI to get their willingness to provide the
requirement. However, due to some unavoidable circumstances from MARDI they conveyed that
the above trainings can be arranged in 2020. Meantime, few letters were exchange between
SLCARP and MARDI regarding formulation of the Technical Management Committee (TMC)
and Visit of the Director General of MARDI to Sri Lanka. A council approved was sought by
SLCARP to nominate the eligible committee members representing Sri Lanka for the TMC align
with the MoU.

MoU between SLCARP and Bangladesh Agricultural Research Council

Memorandum of Understanding (MoU) between the Sri Lanka Council for Agricultural Research
Policy (SLCARP), Sri Lanka and the Bangladesh Agricultural Research Council (BARC), signed
on 18 April 2011 in Bangladesh. Under this programme short term trainings were granted on;Study
Visits and Training Programme, Exchange of Germplasm and Information on Agriculture,
Exchange of Technology and Experts.The discussed work plan 2017 -2021 was then signed in
presence of H.E. Mr. Riaz Hamidullah, High Commissioner of the People’s Republic of
Bangladesh to Sri Lanka, and senior members of NARS at a function. According to the work plan,
both the parties agrees upon to Exchange of Technology, Germplasm and Information, Scientists

and Trainees including institutional collaboration.

ACHIEVEMENTS OF SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT GOALS (SDG) - 2019

In the year 2019, under the National Agricultural Research Plan (NARP), 53 research projects
were coordinated to achieve SDGs relevant to “zero hunger” and “climate change” and Ten (15)
new projects had been recommended for funding in the year 2020. In the programme of Funding
of Inter-institutional research projects, four research projects were coordinated to achieve SDGs.
Other than that one workshop was conducted to develop policies and strategies to mitigate
landslides using bio engineering methods. Experts from National Building Research Organization
(NBRO), Departments, Research Institutes and NGO shared their experiences to develop research

proposal to find out bio engineering methods to mitigate landslides in Sri Lanka

ACKNOWLEDGEMENTS

Sir Lanka Council for Agricultural Research Policy is grateful to its entire staff for their hard
work and cooperation provided in implementing the accelerated work programme. If not for their
continuous cooperation and commitment, the volume of work completed in the 2019 could never
have been achieved. Our sincere thanks are also due to the Chairman and members of the Council

for the valuable support and cooperation extended throughout the year.

SLCARP is also thankful to Hon. Minister of Agriculture, Rural Economic Affairs, Livestock
Development, Irrigation and Fisheries and Aquatic Resources Development, Hon. State Minister
of Agriculture, Hon. Deputy Minister of Agriculture, the Secretary, Ministry of Agriculture,
Secretary of State Ministry of Agriculture, Additional Secretaries, Chief Accountant, Directors
and other staff in the Ministry of Agriculture, Rural Economic Affairs, Livestock Development,
Irrigation and Fisheries and Aquatic Resources Development and those of the Audit Unit for
their excellent cooperation provided to SLCARP for successful completion of year 2019 work

plan.

The cooperation extended by the State Sector Institutions, Universities and relevant Private

Sector Organizations are also acknowledged with thanks.

SLCARP Annual Report 2019

PARTI

16.1.1 Basis of Preparation

a)

b)

a)

Statement of compliance - The financial statement of the council comprise
the Statement of Financial Position, Statement of Financial Performance;
Cash flow statement and notes to the financial statement.

The financial statement was authorized for issue by the Council on 27&
February 2020.

Reporting  entity - The institute of Sti Lanka Council for Agricultural
Research Policy has.been registered under the Parliament act.No.47 of 1987
on 27th of December 1987. The registered office of the council is situated
at No.114/09, Vidya Mawatha, Colombo 07, Sri Lanka.

Principle activities and nature of operations - SLCARP was established
in 1987, under the Act No.47 of 1987 to ensure that agricultural research is
directed towards national development through formulation of agricultural
research policy, research prioritization, planning, facilitation, co-ordination,
monitoring and evaluation of agricultural research.

A Description of the Nature of the Entity - Sri Lanka Council for
Agricultural Research Policy is an umbrella organization of the National
Agricultural Research System (NARS) that operates within several
Ministries. SLCARP came into existence on the 22nd December 1987 to
Create an environment for more productive agricultural research.

SLCARP's mission is to enhance and mobilize the scientific resources in Sri
Lanka efficiently to catalyze and agricultural research and technology
generation within NARS,

With the Secretariat in Colombo, SLCARP serves as an organization in an
advisory Capacity for co-coordinating and consolidating efforts within Sri
Lanka NARS, funding research projects/programmers and promoting scientific
research linkages in prioritized areas both nationally and internationally. CARP
has been instrumental in promoting and facilitating research, by improving and
enhancing agricultural research through documentation and communicating
latest advances in research to the NARS scientists. SLCARP has identified its

"க     4
மா கவி,


SLCARP Annual Report 2019

own perspective, plans and programs for the future in keeping with the
aspirations and goals of the Ministry of Agriculture Development and Agrarian
Services to meet the future challenges in enhancing domestic food production
and exports focused on poverty reduction.

f) Our Vision - A vibrant and sustainable agricultural research, development
and innovation system assuring socio- economic development of Sri Lanka.

8 Our Mission .- To ensure agricultural research, development and
innovations are directed towards national development goals through policy
formulation, facilitation, coordination, monitoring and evaluation and
impact assessment.                                                    |

h) Our Mandated Functions - SLCARP

(1) To advice the Government on all matters regarding the organization, C0
ordination, planning and execution of agricultural research and such other
related matters as may be referred to it by the Minister;

(2) to formulate  national agricultural research policy and priorities;

(3) to define the overall aims and  scope of agricultural research with a view
to furthering national development objectives;

(4) to make recommendations to the appropriate authorities on the financial,
manpower and physical resources required by  agricultural research
institutions and establishments and on the terms and conditions Of service
of the staff of such institutions and establishments;

(5) to review Institutional and departmental agricultural research programmes
and make recommendations with regard to their priorities and funding to
the Ministry of the Minister in charge of the subject of Finance and
Planning,

(6) to promote and facilitate excellence in agricultural résearch;

(7) to act as a channel of communication between agricultural research
institutions and the Government;

(8) to arrange for and fund inter-institutional agricultural research projects;

19               A


SLCARP Annual Report 2019 '

(9) to arrange for and fund special scientific services for the entire agricultural
research sector;

(10)to promote linkage between agricultural research institutions at national and
international level;

(11)Organize conferences and seminars on international, national and inter
Institutional issues relating to the agricultural research,

(12)to arrange for the post-graduate training of agricultural research Staff and
for interchange of sci€ntists with recognized research institutions abroad;
and

(13)to review the performance of agricultural research projects, institutions and
divisions from time to time.

16.1.2. National Agricultural Research Plan (NARP)

National Agricultural Research Plan (NARP) is on of the mandatory functions
conducted by Sri Lanka Council for Agricultural Research Policy under the
programme no 1 and 13 of the Action Plan. Under this programme SLCARP does
the recommendation of research .project proposals for funding, monitoring Of
ongoing projects and evaluating of the terminal reports. Main objective of this.
programme is to facilitate Agricultural research by providing funds, monitoring
ongoing projects and evaluating of terminal reports of these projects.

Annually, end of the year, SLCARP prepares NARP, the document containing all
the details of the research projects to be conducted in the following year. The
projects are implemented by the institutions of the National Agricultural Research
System (NARS) and agriculture related Faculties of the National Universities.
Currently NARP is operated in the Department of Agriculture, Department of
Export Agriculture, and agriculture related Faculties of National Universities.
These projects are designed in accordance with the priority areas identified by Sri
Lanka Council for Agricultural Research Policy for a particular period.



SLCARP Annual Report 2019

16.1.3. Capacity Building Programme

SLCARP decided to revitalize Human Resources Development for the, NARS as
there was a felt requirement for training officers to M.Sc. and PhD level. Thus,
SLCARP submitted a proposal to the Ministry of Agriculture for Capacity Building
of the Researchers of the NARS for which Cabinet Memorandum was issued on
21 September 2017 under the heading of Directing of Researchers of the NARS
for Foreign postgraduate degree training.

This programme provides provision for training to address the training requirement
of the National Agriculture Research System of this country, which needs much
strengthening to meet the challengers of the sector and to be in par with the
neighboring countries in the region.

Number of Candidates who have received admission under the Capacity Building
long term training Programme of SLCARP in year 2019 and on-going scholars of
the Capacity Development Programme.

16.2.2 Basis of MASUTéMEn

16.3

The financial statements have been prepared on the historical cash basis. No
adjustment has been made for inflationary factors in the financial statement.

Functional and presentation of currency
The financial statement of the year end 2010 were presented in Sti Lankan rupees

(LKRs.) and nearest cents.

21


SLCARP Annual Report 2019

However we have decided to present our Financial Statement in LKRs. And round
to the nearest rupee which is effective from the financial year January 01“ 2011
and ahead. Year 2017 was presented in LKRs. and rounded to the nearest rupee.

The stipend and University fees relating to Capacity Building program are paid in
USD ($) where that Expenses is converted to LKR at the spot rate of transaction
date and prepaid the stipend and University fees are taken in to financial
statements at the rate of Balance sheet rate. The difference arisen due to Changes
on Exchange rate has been taken in to financial statements as exchange gain Or
Loss.

16.4 Accounting for Govt. Grants disclose of Govt. Assistance

(a) Accounting for Government Grants & Disclosure of Government Assistance is
adopted.

(Dd) We further say, that accounting policy had been adopted with regard to the

government grants was the method of capital approach but that government grant
was related to the fixed assets it had been taken to the accounts under the method
of income approach.

(Cc) A Deferred Income Fund has been identified only in respect of the assets purchased
 during the year 2018 in the Financial Statements of 2018

16.4.1 Capital Grants (Treasury Grants Research)

According to the Sri Lanka Council for Agricultural Research Policy Act No.14 of
1987_all the Grants received need to be credited to CARP Fund and all the

expenses need to be done out ofthat. In that Sense Capital Grants (Treasury Grants
Research) need to be a considered as a supplementary Note to the CARP Fundand

the remaining balance need to be reflected in the CARP Fund each Year. Then only
Carp Fund will be remaining as an Equity Fund in Statement of Financial Position.

From 2010 to 2017 the funds that were used to purchase of fixed assets have not
been reflected in the Capital Grants (Treasury Grants Research). But a
depreciation income had been transferred to the Statements of Comprehensive
Income. Because of that cumulative adverse effect over last years a negative

balance in CARP fund was visible in Capital Grants (Treasury Grants Research)
in2017 & 2018.



SLCARP Annual Report 2019

Corrective Adiustments have been made in order to rectify above adverse effect
based on the issues emphasized by the Auditors General by.his queries dated

21.12.2019 with the reference of AGL/E/CARP/2018/03.

I Summary areas that were r cognized by the Auditor General is as lows

1. Treasury Grants Research

Inthe years of 2017 & 2018 Treasury Grants Research has reflected negative
balances.
a) Council have made capital expenses more than Fund received for the
activities in Capital nature in 2015, 2017 & 2018.
b) Iwas doubtful the manner of expenses that were incurred on fixed assets
without reflecting such expenses in Treasury Grants Research as that is in

capital nature.
¢) The depreciation inpact of Non- Consumables has also affected to the
negative balance in Treasury Grants Research.

2. The Amortization of the funds received on behalf of Fixed Assets have not been

happened according to the requirements of LKAS 20, Accountin  ng for Government
Grants & Disclosure of Government Assistance as the funds used for those fixed

assets purchases are not reflected in Treasury Grants Research.
3. According to the Sri Lanka Council for Agricultural Research Policy Act No.14 of

1987,_all the Grants received need to be credited to CARP Fund and all the
expenses need to be done out of that.

In order to rectif the above the initial entries that had been passed to Accumulated
Surplus or Deficit (Prior Year Adjustments), Carp Fund & Gift were reversed in
respective Years and placed the correct entries according to LKAS 20, Accounting

for Government Grants & Disclosure of Government Assistance the Correction

entries. Calculation and the explanatory notes are attached as Annexure.

16.4.2 Research Management Activities

Generally, the Capital Fund are utilizing to Research Management Activities where the
requirements of LKAS 38 for Intangible assets are not comply with. Hence the Research

management activities are in a nature where that could not be capitalize. Due to that

reason both the expense_and amount of Fund are shown in the Comprehensive Income
Statement in order to reflect the effect.

Lanka, However, some of the research institutes/ Universities do not settle this research
imprest at the year-end such amount stated as an unsettled research imprest.

1.6 Stocks

Stocks are shown in the financial statement at lower of market value or purchase price.
Thé stock is valued using FIFO method. The Non Consumables are classified as stock item
based on the nature of that category which was previously presented in Property plant and
equipment. The Depreciation provided so far is reversed back to Prior Year Adjustments.

National Audit Office

AGL/E/CARP/01/19/03                                                                                              13 August 2020

Chairman

Sri Lanka Council for Agricultural Research Policy

The Auditor General's Report as per 12** sentence of the National Audit Act bearing

number 19 of 2018 on Financial Statements of the Sri Lanka Council for Agricultural

Research Policy for the year ending by 31 December 2019

1.
1.1

Financial Statements

Qualified Opinion

Balance Sheet of the Sri Lanka Council for Agricultural Research Policy by date of 31
December 2019 and the Comprehensive Income Statement for the year ending by that
date, Equity Changing Statements and Cash Flow Statement for the year ending by that
date and Notes relevant to Financial Statements, Financial Statements with summarized
important accounting principles for the year ending by 31 December 2019 had been
audited under my execution in accordance with the regulations of the National Audit Act
No. 19 of 2018 and the Financial Act No. 38 of 1971 which should be read in conjunction
with 154 (1) article of the Constitution of the Democratic Socialist Republic of Sri
Lanka. In accordance with the regulations of the 154 (6) article of the Constitution, my

Report will be tabled in the Parliament in due course.

Except the impact of the issues detailed in the part of the Basis for the Qualified Opinion
of my Report, 1 am of the opinion that the financial status of the Sri Lanka Council for
Agricultural Research Policy as at 31 December 2019 and its financial activities and
cash flows for the year ending by that date are expressing true and reliable status

according to the accounting standards of the public sector of Sri Lanka.


1.2 Basis for the Qualified Opinion

(a) Though the 04 motor cars of which the cost was Rupees 26,321,295 and which were
completely depreciated at the end of the reviewed year were Still in use, action had not
been taken to show reliable value of those Vehicles in Financial Statements, after
revaluation of vehicles considering the effective life span of those according to Sri Lanka

Public Sector Accounting Standards No. 3.

(b) Foradding of a new part to the building in which the Sri Lanka Council for Agricultural
Research Policy is located, the advance money of Rupees 2,460,000 paid to the Building
Department in the reviewed year, had been shown under Non-current Assets as

incomplete work instead of showing under Current Assets in the Balance Sheet.

(C) As the total sumofRupees 473,770 which consisted the course fees paid by the Institution
for the officers who were overseas for study activities and the Bank charges and
Commission money Charged by the Bank had not been matched to the expenditure of the
reviewed year, the balance of the reviewed year had excessively been shown by that

amount.

I have conducted the Audit in accordance with the Sri Lanka Audit Standards. My
responsibilities under these Audit Standards are further detailed in this Report, in the Part of
Auditor's responsibility in connection with the auditing of Financial Statements. It is my belief
that the audit evidences obtained by me are sufficient and appropriate for the providing of a

basis for my qualified opinion.

1.3 Responsibility of the Management and the Governing Parties on Financial

Statements

Preparation of these Financial Statements according to Accounting Standards of the Sri
Lanka Public Sector, submission in reliable form and deciding of required internal
controls which create possibilities to prepare Financial Statements without significant
incorrect statements which would derive due to frauds and errors, are the responsibilities

of the Management.


1.4

In preparation of the Financial Statements, it is responsibility of the Management to decide
the possibility of the continued functioning of the Sri Lanka Council for Agricultural
Research Policy. Except if the Management considers to liquidate the Council or to cease
functioning when there is no other option, it is the responsibility of the Management to
maintain accounts and to disclose issues related to the continued functioning of the

Council being on the basis of continued functioning.

The responsibility on the financial reporting activity is taken by the Governing Parties.

Books! ledgers and reports of the Institution on incomes, expenditure, assets and liabilities
should be maintained properly so that it would be possible to prepare the annual and
periodical Financial Statements in accordance with the 16 (1) sub sentence of the National

Audit Act No. 19 of 2018.

Auditors responsibility on auditing of Financial Statements

Providing a reliable confirmation that as a whole, Financial Statements do not contain
significant incorrect statements occurring due to frauds and errors and issuing of Auditor's
Report inclusive of my opinion are my objectives. Even though the reliable confirmation
is a confirmation of high level, when the auditing is conducted according to Sri Lanka
Audit Standards, it would not always a confirmation that would reveal the significant mis-
statements. Significant mis-statements may occur due to frauds and errors which would
affect alone or together and it is expected that these would be an impact on the economic

decisions taken by referees based on these Financial Statements.

Auditing has been conducted by me in accordance with the Sri Lanka Audit Standards

with judgment and suspicion based on my professional capacity. Also,

 When identifying and assessing risks of significantly incorrect statements which may
occur in Financial Statements due to frauds or errors, by planning of appropriate
auditing procedures suitable to situation to overcome the risks which may occur due
to frauds and errors, obtaining of sufficient and proper audit evidences makes the basis

of my opinion. The impact which occurs by a fraud is stronger than an impact which


takes place from significant incorrect Statements. Collusion, preparation of false

documents, intentional ignoring or ignoring of internal governances cause frauds.

s For the purpose of formulation of auditing procedures suitable to situation, an
understanding on internal governance of the Council had been obtained, but there is

no intention to express an opinion on the effectiveness of the internal governance.

e Reliability ofthe accounting principles and the accounting estimates which have been
used and the appropriateness of the disclosures made by the Management in

connection were evaluated.

 1n connection with the fact that on the grounds of incidents and conditions whether
there is a significant uncertainty on the continued functioning of the Council, based
on the obtained audit evidences, the relevance of the adopting of the basis on the
continued functioning of the Institution had been decided for accounting. 1f 1 conclude
that there is a significant uncertainty, emphasis of my Audit Report should be given
to the relevant disclosures in the Financial Statements. 1f those disclosures are not
sufficient, my opinion should be modified. However, continued functioning may Cease

on future incidents or conditions.

e The submission, Structure and the content of the Financial Statements in which the
disclosures are included were evaluated and the fact that the transactions and incidents
which made basis for those are included in Financial Statements appropriately and in

reliable form had been evaluated.

Governing Parties were made aware of the important audit findings, main internal governing

weaknesses and other issues which were identified in my audit.

2. Report on other Legal and Regulatory Requirements

Special provisions connected to the requirements stated below are included in the National

Audit Act No. 19 of 2018.


In accordance with the requirements Stated in the 12 (1) sentence of the National Audit
Act No. 19 of 2018, except the impact occurring by the issues detailed in the Part on
Basis for the Opinion of my Report, all information and explanations needed for the
audit have been obtained by me and, as shown by my investigation, Council has

maintained the appropriate Financial Reports.

According to the requirement Stated in the 6 (1) (1) (iii) sentence of the National Audit
Act No. 19 of 2018, Financial Statements of the Council which have been submitted

tally with those of the previous year.

According to the requirement stated in the 6 (1) (11) (iv) sentence of the National Audit
Act No. 19 of 2018, the recommendations made by me in the previous year have been

included in the Financial Statements which have been submitted.

On procedures followed and evidences obtained and in limitations to the significant issues, my

attention had not been taken by anything which leads to the making of below mentioned

statements.

According to the requirement Stated in the 12 (1) sentence of the National Audit Act
No. 19 of 2018, certain member of the Governing Board of the Council, with the
involvement of the Council, there had been an involvement exclusive of general

business condition, directly or in other way, pertaining to certain contract.

According to the requirement Stated in the 12 (1) sentence of the National Audit Act
No. 19 of 2018, has acted not adhering to a certain written rule or some other Common

or specific orders issued by the Governing Board of the Council.

According to the requirement stated in the 12 (1) sentence of the National Audit Act
No. 19 of 2018, has acted not adhering to the powers, functions or activities of the

Council

According to the requirement Stated in the 12 (1) sentence of the National Audit Act
No. 19 of 2018, resources of the Council had not been procured and utilized
economically, efficiently and effectively in accordance with the rules and regulations

in the relevant time periods.


3.

Other Audit Observations

(a)

(C)

Despite the identification of the importance of the emphasis to be given to the
Organic Agriculture by the Council, and introducing to research institutions of Sri
Lanka 07 priority areas in which the research should be increased, the research on
organic agricultural policy, quality status of the organic foods available in the

present market had not been conducted from year 2017 onwards.

Though the information on number of research conducted in agricultural research
institutions, financial allocations provided for research, information on researcher,
scientist and other staff and physical resources belong to the institution had been
collected up to the reviewed year, updating of the database system (Information for
Agricultural Research Managers) after year 2106 and issuing of the publications
which contain these information and which should be issued annually, had not been

done after year 2010.

According to the Contractual Agreement between Bangladesh Agricultural
Research Council, Malaysian Agricultural Research Council and the Sri Lanka
Council for Agricultural Research Policy initiated in years 2011 and 2016,
arrangement of overseas short-term training for 10 officers under the exchange of
consultants and scientists in the field of agriculture had been included in the Action
Plan of 2019. But the Council had not taken action to identify such training

opportunities and to direct officers to the same.

Though it has been mentioned that the researchers who undergo training under the
overseas post graduate degree programme should select their research themes,
giving emphasis to the problems and constraints to which agriculture sector of Sri
Lanka is facing now or is likely to face in future, number of officers who had
selected fields of agricultural mechanization and organic agriculture which have
been identified as fields to be improved for the benefit of the agriculture sector of
Sri Lanka was at a very low level. However, the Institution has not implemented

planned procedures to improve this condition.


(e) Though it had been planned to provide funds for 06 projects consisting 02 projects
selected from the research proposals called from research institutions in year 2019
and 04 projects carried forward from past years, funds had been allocated in the
year reviewed for 03 projects at Tea Research Institute which had been commenced
in years 2017 and 2018 and not yet been completed and also for 01 project of the
Department of Agriculture. Officers of the Council had not taken action to
physically examine the performance of each of these projects and also new

proposals pertaining to the reviewed year had not been identified.

(f) Due tothe reason of not taking action on recruitment of research officers of existing
research institutions, the number of research conducted in four fields — Floriculture,
Forestry, Agricultural Mechanization, Natural Resources Management has been

reduced by 378 in year 2019 relative to the year 2017.

(J) From the funds granted to four research institutions and two universities for
research activities, a sum of Rupees 659,131 which should be settled to the Council
had not yet been recovered and is carried forward in accounts from year 2006

onwards.

(h) A sum of Rupees 192,890 which had been deposited by several private institutions
on providing of services during the period from 2016 to 2018, had not been released

and is carried forward in accounts.

(1) As action has not been taken also in the year reviewed for the recruitment for the
Vacancies in 36 approved cadre positions which exist for several years, main 05
positions of the Institution, i.e. the positions of Senior Scientist, Senior Research

Officer, Accountant, Administrative Officer and Librarian remained vacant.

Ww P C Wickramaratne

SLCARP Annual Report 2019

Annual Report 2019 - Summary Report

Sri Lanka Council for Agricultural Research Policy

Performance of the Institution

SLCARP organized National Awards for the excellence in Agricultural Research to
recognize the outstanding achievement in agricultural research on 28 October 2019.
Awards were given to the 10 excellence research teams who were from Plantation, Non-

Plantation and Fisheries sectors.

The international Workshop on Underutilized Fish and Marine Genetic Resources and their
Amelioration was organized in collaboration with Asia — Pacific Association Of
Agricultural Research Institutions (APAARI) 10- 12 July, 2019 at National Aquatic
Resource Agency (NARA)..

Under the Human Resources Development program, further selections were made and 23
candidates were selected to be sent in year 2019, for training in Thailand, Malaysia, and
Philippines Universities for 2019.

Two Research Institutes were reviewed in 2019 by panels of external reviewers appointed
by SLCARP. They were Coconut Research Institute (CRI) & National Plant Quarantine
Service (NPQS) of the Department of Agriculture (DOA). Review committee reports were
submitted to the Council and to the respective institutes.

The action taken to rectify the deficiencies indicated in audit queries and audit reports

Action has been taken to recalculate the value of 04 vehicles owned by the council
considering the effective lifespan.

A letter has been sent to the Secretary to the Ministry of Agriculture requesting necessary
instructions for the recruitment process

Refundable deposits are released upon request by the deposited institutions.

The midterm actions proposed to be taken

All Staff have been instructed to follow manifesto of the government to improve the
Council’s performance.
